12:I[27936,["/_next/static/chunks/08u3pj27txr.q.js","/_next/static/chunks/090hefefkaym5.js","/_next/static/chunks/0d3shmwh5_nmn.js","/_next/static/chunks/0uzjgq-bziqbz.js","/_next/static/chunks/0gcdigp4wgr~4.js","/_next/static/chunks/0n4eo6ldx1_9y.js","/_next/static/chunks/138gjkqa370op.js"],"WikiTopicClient"]
7:["$","main",null,{"className":"wiki-main wiki-main--wide","children":["$","$9",null,{"fallback":["$","div",null,{"style":{"padding":"2rem","textAlign":"center"},"children":"Loading topic..."}],"children":["$","$L12",null,{"topic":{"slug":"chunked-prefill","title":"Chunked Prefill","summary":"A serving-time technique that breaks the long prefill of a prompt into small chunks and interleaves them with decode steps of other requests. By keeping GPU utilisation high during prefill and avoiding long tail latencies, chunked prefill dramatically improves throughput in mixed-batch LLM serving.","domain":"llm","level":"advanced","type":"mixed","tags":["advanced","implementation","ml","product","path-transformer-llm","path-scaling-advanced"],"prerequisites":["key-value-kv-caching","pagedattention"],"related":["disaggregated-prefill-decode-serving","paged-vs-block-kv-cache","pagedattention"],"updatedAt":"2026-04-17","sourceDeck":"Machine Learning by Henrik Nordberg","papers":[{"citation":"2023 · Amey Agrawal et al. · SARATHI: Efficient LLM Inference by Piggybacking Decodes with Chunked Prefills","url":"https://arxiv.org/abs/2308.16369"}],"sections":[{"kind":"prose","body":"<p>LLM inference has two distinct phases. <b>Prefill</b> processes the entire prompt in parallel and is <b>compute-bound</b> (the attention and MLP matmuls saturate tensor cores). <b>Decode</b> generates tokens one at a time and is <b>memory-bandwidth-bound</b> (per-token compute is small but requires reading the full KV cache). Naively interleaving them causes problems: a long prefill blocks all ongoing decode requests, spiking tail latency.</p>"},{"kind":"prose","title":"The idea","body":"<p>Chunked prefill (SARATHI, Agrawal et al., 2023) splits the prefill of a single request into chunks of size \\( c \\) tokens and schedules each chunk in the same batch as the decode tokens of other requests. Because prefill and decode are limited by different resources, they <b>piggyback</b> onto the same GPU step:</p>\n<ul>\n  <li>Prefill chunks use excess tensor-core FLOPs.</li>\n  <li>Decode tokens use excess HBM bandwidth.</li>\n  <li>Combined, they consume both resources more fully than either phase alone.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Typical chunk size: \\( c = 512 \\) tokens, balancing granularity (fewer blocks = lower scheduling overhead) against decode latency (bigger chunks delay decodes).</p>"},{"kind":"prose","title":"Effects in production","body":"<ul>\n  <li><b>Throughput up 2–3×</b> at matching median latency vs naive batching (vLLM, DeepSpeed-MII report similar gains).</li>\n  <li><b>Tail latency down sharply.</b> A long prompt can no longer block short-prompt decodes behind it; the decode SLO becomes decoupled from prompt-length distribution.</li>\n  <li><b>Works with PagedAttention.</b> Chunked prefill writes into the same paged KV cache; each chunk appends new pages.</li>\n</ul>"},{"kind":"pitfall","title":"Caveats","body":"<ul>\n  <li><b>Chunk size tuning.</b> Too small ⇒ scheduler overhead dominates. Too large ⇒ decode latency spikes whenever a prefill chunk runs. The sweet spot is hardware- and model-dependent.</li>\n  <li><b>Attention cost across chunks.</b> The \\( k \\)-th prefill chunk must attend to the previous \\( (k-1) \\) chunks (the context prefix grows), so per-chunk compute scales linearly with position. This is not a regression vs full prefill; it is just re-accounted.</li>\n  <li><b>Speculative decoding interplay.</b> With speculative decoding, a \"decode\" step actually runs several candidate tokens; the prefill/decode mix becomes less bimodal and piggyback gains shrink.</li>\n  <li><b>Alternative: disaggregated serving</b> — running prefill and decode on separate GPUs entirely — provides even better isolation at the cost of extra KV-cache transfer.</li>\n</ul>"}],"cards":[{"noteId":"chunked-prefill-mech","prompt":"Why does chunked prefill improve serving throughput even though it performs the same total compute as a monolithic prefill?","answer":"<p>Prefill is tensor-core-bound while decode is memory-bandwidth-bound. By interleaving prefill chunks with decode tokens in the same GPU step, the batch simultaneously saturates two different resources — tensor cores (via the prefill matmuls) and HBM bandwidth (via the decode's KV-cache reads). Overall resource utilisation rises, so throughput at matching latency improves 2–3× compared with running phases back-to-back.</p>","tags":["advanced","implementation","ml","product","path-transformer-llm"]},{"noteId":"chunked-prefill-pitfall","prompt":"What happens to tail latency if the prefill chunk size is set too large (e.g., 4096) in chunked-prefill serving, and why?","answer":"<p>Tail latency spikes: whenever a long-prompt request enters the scheduler, its first prefill chunk monopolises a full GPU step, delaying all interleaved decode tokens by the prefill-chunk time. Smaller chunks (e.g., 256–512) bound the maximum delay a decode token can experience regardless of prompt length — the core latency guarantee of chunked prefill.</p>","tags":["advanced","implementation","ml","product","path-transformer-llm"]},{"noteId":"chunked-prefill-contrast","prompt":"Contrast chunked prefill with disaggregated prefill/decode serving in terms of isolation and engineering cost.","answer":"<p>Chunked prefill keeps both phases on the same GPU and interleaves them temporally; simple to deploy, no KV-cache movement, but the two phases still compete for resources. Disaggregated serving runs prefill on dedicated GPUs and decode on separate GPUs, transferring the KV cache across them; provides full isolation and is often faster at scale but requires extra engineering for cache transfer and cluster scheduling.</p>","tags":["advanced","implementation","ml","product","path-transformer-llm"]},{"noteId":"chunked-prefill-app","prompt":"SARATHI coined the term \"piggybacking\" in the context of chunked prefill. What two workloads are piggybacking onto each other, and what bottleneck resource does each use?","answer":"<p>A <b>prefill chunk</b> (compute-bound on tensor-core FLOPs) piggybacks onto a set of <b>decode steps</b> (memory-bandwidth-bound on HBM reads of the KV cache). Each phase consumes the resource the other does not need; running them together fills both, whereas running each alone leaves one resource idle — the essence of the piggyback speedup.</p>","tags":["advanced","implementation","ml","product","path-transformer-llm"]}]},"manifest":{"version":1,"updatedAt":"2026-04-25","sourceDeck":"Machine Learning by Henrik Nordberg","topics":[{"slug":"linear-regression-basics","title":"Linear regression basics","summary":"Linear regression fits an affine function to predict a continuous target by minimizing squared residuals between predictions and observed values.
